## Skill: remotion-best-practices

**Base directory**: /Users/qua/projects/skills-launch-video/.opencode/skills/remotion-best-practices

## When to use

Use this skills whenever you are dealing with Remotion code to obtain the domain-specific knowledge.

## How to use

Read individual rule files for detailed explanations and code examples:

- [rules/3d.md](rules/3d.md) - 3D content in Remotion using Three.js and React Three Fiber
- [rules/animations.md](rules/animations.md) - Fundamental animation skills for Remotion
- [rules/assets.md](rules/assets.md) - Importing images, videos, audio, and fonts into Remotion
- [rules/audio.md](rules/audio.md) - Using audio and sound in Remotion - importing, trimming, volume, speed, pitch
- [rules/calculate-metadata.md](rules/calculate-metadata.md) - Dynamically set composition duration, dimensions, and props
- [rules/can-decode.md](rules/can-decode.md) - Check if a video can be decoded by the browser using Mediabunny
- [rules/charts.md](rules/charts.md) - Chart and data visualization patterns for Remotion
- [rules/compositions.md](rules/compositions.md) - Defining compositions, stills, folders, default props and dynamic metadata
- [rules/display-captions.md](rules/display-captions.md) - Displaying captions in Remotion with TikTok-style pages and word highlighting
- [rules/extract-frames.md](rules/extract-frames.md) - Extract frames from videos at specific timestamps using Mediabunny
- [rules/fonts.md](rules/fonts.md) - Loading Google Fonts and local fonts in Remotion
- [rules/get-audio-duration.md](rules/get-audio-duration.md) - Getting the duration of an audio file in seconds with Mediabunny
- [rules/get-video-dimensions.md](rules/get-video-dimensions.md) - Getting the width and height of a video file with Mediabunny
- [rules/get-video-duration.md](rules/get-video-duration.md) - Getting the duration of a video file in seconds with Mediabunny
- [rules/gifs.md](rules/gifs.md) - Displaying GIFs synchronized with Remotion's timeline
- [rules/images.md](rules/images.md) - Embedding images in Remotion using the Img component
- [rules/import-srt-captions.md](rules/import-srt-captions.md) - Importing .srt subtitle files into Remotion using @remotion/captions
- [rules/lottie.md](rules/lottie.md) - Embedding Lottie animations in Remotion
- [rules/measuring-dom-nodes.md](rules/measuring-dom-nodes.md) - Measuring DOM element dimensions in Remotion
- [rules/measuring-text.md](rules/measuring-text.md) - Measuring text dimensions, fitting text to containers, and checking overflow
- [rules/sequencing.md](rules/sequencing.md) - Sequencing patterns for Remotion - delay, trim, limit duration of items
- [rules/tailwind.md](rules/tailwind.md) - Using TailwindCSS in Remotion
- [rules/text-animations.md](rules/text-animations.md) - Typography and text animation patterns for Remotion
- [rules/timing.md](rules/timing.md) - Interpolation curves in Remotion - linear, easing, spring animations
- [rules/transcribe-captions.md](rules/transcribe-captions.md) - Transcribing audio to generate captions in Remotion
- [rules/transitions.md](rules/transitions.md) - Scene transition patterns for Remotion
- [rules/trimming.md](rules/trimming.md) - Trimming patterns for Remotion - cut the beginning or end of animations
- [rules/videos.md](rules/videos.md) - Embedding videos in Remotion - trimming, volume, speed, looping, pitch

00005|   tags: typography, text, typewriter, highlighter ken
00006| ---
00007| 
00008| ## Text animations
00009| 
00010| Based on `useCurrentFrame()`, reduce the string character by character to create a typewriter effect.
00011| 
00012| ## Typewriter Effect
00013| 
00014| See [Typewriter](assets/text-animations-typewriter.tsx) for an advanced example with a blinking cursor and a pause after the first sentence.
00015| 
00016| Always use string slicing for typewriter effects. Never use per-character opacity.
00017| 
00018| ## Word Highlighting
00019| 
00020| See [Word Highlight](assets/text-animations-word-highlight.tsx) for an example for how a word highlight is animated, like with a highlighter pen.

<file>
00001| ---
00002| name: transitions
00003| description: Fullscreen scene transitions for Remotion.
00004| metadata:
00005|   tags: transitions, fade, slide, wipe, scenes
00006| ---
00007| 
00008| ## Fullscreen transitions
00009| 
00010| Using `<TransitionSeries>` to animate between multiple scenes or clips.  
00011| This will absolutely position the children.
00012| 
00013| ## Prerequisites
00014| 
00015| First, the @remotion/transitions package needs to be installed.  
00016| If it is not, use the following command:
00017| 
00018| ```bash
00019| npx remotion add @remotion/transitions # If project uses npm
00020| bunx remotion add @remotion/transitions # If project uses bun
00021| yarn remotion add @remotion/transitions # If project uses yarn
00022| pnpm exec remotion add @remotion/transitions # If project uses pnpm
00023| ```
00024| 
00025| ## Example usage
00026| 
00027| ```tsx
00028| import {TransitionSeries, linearTiming} from '@remotion/transitions';
00029| import {fade} from '@remotion/transitions/fade';
00030| 
00031| <TransitionSeries>
00032|   <TransitionSeries.Sequence durationInFrames={60}>
00033|     <SceneA />
00034|   </TransitionSeries.Sequence>
00035|   <TransitionSeries.Transition presentation={fade()} timing={linearTiming({durationInFrames: 15})} />
00036|   <TransitionSeries.Sequence durationInFrames={60}>
00037|     <SceneB />
00038|   </TransitionSeries.Sequence>
00039| </TransitionSeries>;
00040| ```
00041| 
00042| ## Available Transition Types
00043| 
00044| Import transitions from their respective modules:
00045| 
00046| ```tsx
00047| import {fade} from '@remotion/transitions/fade';
00048| import {slide} from '@remotion/transitions/slide';
00049| import {wipe} from '@remotion/transitions/wipe';
00050| import {flip} from '@remotion/transitions/flip';
00051| import {clockWipe} from '@remotion/transitions/clock-wipe';
00052| ```
00053| 
00054| ## Slide Transition with Direction
00055| 
00056| Specify slide direction for enter/exit animations.
00057| 
00058| ```tsx
00059| import {slide} from '@remotion/transitions/slide';
00060| 
00061| <TransitionSeries.Transition presentation={slide({direction: 'from-left'})} timing={linearTiming({durationInFrames: 20})} />;
00062| ```
00063| 
00064| Directions: `"from-left"`, `"from-right"`, `"from-top"`, `"from-bottom"`
00065| 
00066| ## Timing Options
00067| 
00068| ```tsx
00069| import {linearTiming, springTiming} from '@remotion/transitions';
00070| 
00071| // Linear timing - constant speed
00072| linearTiming({durationInFrames: 20});
00073| 
00074| // Spring timing - organic motion
00075| springTiming({config: {damping: 200}, durationInFrames: 25});
00076| ```
00077| 
00078| ## Duration calculation
00079| 
00080| Transitions overlap adjacent scenes, so the total composition length is **shorter** than the sum of all sequence durations.
00081| 
00082| For example, with two 60-frame sequences and a 15-frame transition:
00083| 
00084| - Without transitions: `60 + 60 = 120` frames
00085| - With transition: `60 + 60 - 15 = 105` frames
00086| 
00087| The transition duration is subtracted because both scenes play simultaneously during the transition.
00088| 
00089| ### Getting the duration of a transition
00090| 
00091| Use the `getDurationInFrames()` method on the timing object:
00092| 
00093| ```tsx
00094| import {linearTiming, springTiming} from '@remotion/transitions';
00095| 
00096| const linearDuration = linearTiming({durationInFrames: 20}).getDurationInFrames({fps: 30});
00097| // Returns 20
00098| 
00099| const springDuration = springTiming({config: {damping: 200}}).getDurationInFrames({fps: 30});
00100| // Returns calculated duration based on spring physics
00101| ```
00102| 
00103| For `springTiming` without an explicit `durationInFrames`, the duration depends on `fps` because it calculates when the spring animation settles.
00104| 
00105| ### Calculating total composition duration
00106| 
00107| ```tsx
00108| import {linearTiming} from '@remotion/transitions';
00109| 
00110| const scene1Duration = 60;
00111| const scene2Duration = 60;
00112| const scene3Duration = 60;
00113| 
00114| const timing1 = linearTiming({durationInFrames: 15});
00115| const timing2 = linearTiming({durationInFrames: 20});
00116| 
00117| const transition1Duration = timing1.getDurationInFrames({fps: 30});
00118| const transition2Duration = timing2.getDurationInFrames({fps: 30});
00119| 
00120| const totalDuration = scene1Duration + scene2Duration + scene3Duration - transition1Duration - transition2Duration;
00121| // 60 + 60 + 60 - 15 - 20 = 145 frames
00122| ```
00123| 

(End of file - total 123 lines)
</file>

<file>
00001| ---
00002| name: timing
00003| description: Interpolation curves in Remotion - linear, easing, spring animations
00004| metadata:
00005|   tags: spring, bounce, easing, interpolation
00006| ---
00007| 
00008| A simple linear interpolation is done using the `interpolate` function.
00009| 
00010| ```ts title="Going from 0 to 1 over 100 frames"
00011| import {interpolate} from 'remotion';
00012| 
00013| const opacity = interpolate(frame, [0, 100], [0, 1]);
00014| ```
00015| 
00016| By default, the values are not clamped, so the value can go outside the range [0, 1].  
00017| Here is how they can be clamped:
00018| 
00019| ```ts title="Going from 0 to 1 over 100 frames with extrapolation"
00020| const opacity = interpolate(frame, [0, 100], [0, 1], {
00021|   extrapolateRight: 'clamp',
00022|   extrapolateLeft: 'clamp',
00023| });
00024| ```
00025| 
00026| ## Spring animations
00027| 
00028| Spring animations have a more natural motion.  
00029| They go from 0 to 1 over time.
00030| 
00031| ```ts title="Spring animation from 0 to 1 over 100 frames"
00032| import {spring, useCurrentFrame, useVideoConfig} from 'remotion';
00033| 
00034| const frame = useCurrentFrame();
00035| const {fps} = useVideoConfig();
00036| 
00037| const scale = spring({
00038|   frame,
00039|   fps,
00040| });
00041| ```
00042| 
00043| ### Physical properties
00044| 
00045| The default configuration is: `mass: 1, damping: 10, stiffness: 100`.  
00046| This leads to the animation having a bit of bounce before it settles.
00047| 
00048| The config can be overwritten like this:
00049| 
00050| ```ts
00051| const scale = spring({
00052|   frame,
00053|   fps,
00054|   config: {damping: 200},
00055| });
00056| ```
00057| 
00058| The recommended configuration for a natural motion without a bounce is: `{ damping: 200 }`.
00059| 
00060| Here are some common configurations:
00061| 
00062| ```tsx
00063| const smooth = {damping: 200}; // Smooth, no bounce (subtle reveals)
00064| const snappy = {damping: 20, stiffness: 200}; // Snappy, minimal bounce (UI elements)
00065| const bouncy = {damping: 8}; // Bouncy entrance (playful animations)
00066| const heavy = {damping: 15, stiffness: 80, mass: 2}; // Heavy, slow, small bounce
00067| ```
00068| 
00069| ### Delay
00070| 
00071| The animation starts immediately by default.  
00072| Use the `delay` parameter to delay the animation by a number of frames.
00073| 
00074| ```tsx
00075| const entrance = spring({
00076|   frame: frame - ENTRANCE_DELAY,
00077|   fps,
00078|   delay: 20,
00079| });
00080| ```
00081| 
00082| ### Duration
00083| 
00084| A `spring()` has a natural duration based on the physical properties.  
00085| To stretch the animation to a specific duration, use the `durationInFrames` parameter.
00086| 
00087| ```tsx
00088| const spring = spring({
00089|   frame,
00090|   fps,
00091|   durationInFrames: 40,
00092| });
00093| ```
00094| 
00095| ### Combining spring() with interpolate()
00096| 
00097| Map spring output (0-1) to custom ranges:
00098| 
00099| ```tsx
00100| const springProgress = spring({
00101|   frame,
00102|   fps,
00103| });
00104| 
00105| // Map to rotation
00106| const rotation = interpolate(springProgress, [0, 1], [0, 360]);
00107| 
00108| <div style={{rotate: rotation + 'deg'}} />;
00109| ```
00110| 
00111| ### Adding springs
00112| 
00113| Springs return just numbers, so math can be performed:
00114| 
00115| ```tsx
00116| const frame = useCurrentFrame();
00117| const {fps, durationInFrames} = useVideoConfig();
00118| 
00119| const inAnimation = spring({
00120|   frame,
00121|   fps,
00122| });
00123| const outAnimation = spring({
00124|   frame,
00125|   fps,
00126|   durationInFrames: 1 * fps,
00127|   delay: durationInFrames - 1 * fps,
00128| });
00129| 
00130| const scale = inAnimation - outAnimation;
00131| ```
00132| 
00133| ## Easing
00134| 
00135| Easing can be added to the `interpolate` function:
00136| 
00137| ```ts
00138| import {interpolate, Easing} from 'remotion';
00139| 
00140| const value1 = interpolate(frame, [0, 100], [0, 1], {
00141|   easing: Easing.inOut(Easing.quad),
00142|   extrapolateLeft: 'clamp',
00143|   extrapolateRight: 'clamp',
00144| });
00145| ```
00146| 
00147| The default easing is `Easing.linear`.  
00148| There are various other convexities:
00149| 
00150| - `Easing.in` for starting slow and accelerating
00151| - `Easing.out` for starting fast and slowing down
00152| - `Easing.inOut`
00153| 
00154| and curves (sorted from most linear to most curved):
00155| 
00156| - `Easing.quad`
00157| - `Easing.sin`
00158| - `Easing.exp`
00159| - `Easing.circle`
00160| 
00161| Convexities and curves need be combined for an easing function:
00162| 
00163| ```ts
00164| const value1 = interpolate(frame, [0, 100], [0, 1], {
00165|   easing: Easing.inOut(Easing.quad),
00166|   extrapolateLeft: 'clamp',
00167|   extrapolateRight: 'clamp',
00168| });
00169| ```
00170| 
00171| Cubic bezier curves are also supported:
00172| 
00173| ```ts
00174| const value1 = interpolate(frame, [0, 100], [0, 1], {
00175|   easing: Easing.bezier(0.8, 0.22, 0.96, 0.65),
00176|   extrapolateLeft: 'clamp',
00177|   extrapolateRight: 'clamp',
00178| });
00179| ```
00180|

<file>
00001| ---
00002| name: sequencing
00003| description: Sequencing patterns for Remotion - delay, trim, limit duration of items
00004| metadata:
00005|   tags: sequence, series, timing, delay, trim
00006| ---
00007| 
00008| Use `<Sequence>` to delay when an element appears in the timeline.
00009| 
00010| ```tsx
00011| import { Sequence } from "remotion";
00012| 
00013| const {fps} = useVideoConfig();
00014| 
00015| <Sequence from={1 * fps} durationInFrames={2 * fps} premountFor={1 * fps}>
00016|   <Title />
00017| </Sequence>
00018| <Sequence from={2 * fps} durationInFrames={2 * fps} premountFor={1 * fps}>
00019|   <Subtitle />
00020| </Sequence>
00021| ```
00022| 
00023| This will by default wrap the component in an absolute fill element.  
00024| If the items should not be wrapped, use the `layout` prop:
00025| 
00026| ```tsx
00027| <Sequence layout="none">
00028|   <Title />
00029| </Sequence>
00030| ```
00031| 
00032| ## Premounting
00033| 
00034| This loads the component in the timeline before it is actually played.  
00035| Always premount any `<Sequence>`!
00036| 
00037| ```tsx
00038| <Sequence premountFor={1 * fps}>
00039|   <Title />
00040| </Sequence>
00041| ```
00042| 
00043| ## Series
00044| 
00045| Use `<Series>` when elements should play one after another without overlap.
00046| 
00047| ```tsx
00048| import {Series} from 'remotion';
00049| 
00050| <Series>
00051|   <Series.Sequence durationInFrames={45}>
00052|     <Intro />
00053|   </Series.Sequence>
00054|   <Series.Sequence durationInFrames={60}>
00055|     <MainContent />
00056|   </Series.Sequence>
00057|   <Series.Sequence durationInFrames={30}>
00058|     <Outro />
00059|   </Series.Sequence>
00060| </Series>;
00061| ```
00062| 
00063| Same as with `<Sequence>`, the items will be wrapped in an absolute fill element by default when using `<Series.Sequence>`, unless the `layout` prop is set to `none`.
00064| 
00065| ### Series with overlaps
00066| 
00067| Use negative offset for overlapping sequences:
00068| 
00069| ```tsx
00070| <Series>
00071|   <Series.Sequence durationInFrames={60}>
00072|     <SceneA />
00073|   </Series.Sequence>
00074|   <Series.Sequence offset={-15} durationInFrames={60}>
00075|     {/* Starts 15 frames before SceneA ends */}
00076|     <SceneB />
00077|   </Series.Sequence>
00078| </Series>
00079| ```
00080| 
00081| ## Frame References Inside Sequences
00082| 
00083| Inside a Sequence, `useCurrentFrame()` returns the local frame (starting from 0):
00084| 
00085| ```tsx
00086| <Sequence from={60} durationInFrames={30}>
00087|   <MyComponent />
00088|   {/* Inside MyComponent, useCurrentFrame() returns 0-29, not 60-89 */}
00089| </Sequence>
00090| ```
00091| 
00092| ## Nested Sequences
00093| 
00094| Sequences can be nested for complex timing:
00095| 
00096| ```tsx
00097| <Sequence from={0} durationInFrames={120}>
00098|   <Background />
00099|   <Sequence from={15} durationInFrames={90} layout="none">
00100|     <Title />
00101|   </Sequence>
00102|   <Sequence from={45} durationInFrames={60} layout="none">
00103|     <Subtitle />
00104|   </Sequence>
00105| </Sequence>
00106| ```
00107| 

(End of file - total 107 lines)
</file>
```

00007| 
00008| # Using fonts in Remotion
00009| 
00010| ## Google Fonts with @remotion/google-fonts
00011| 
00012| The recommended way to use Google Fonts. It's type-safe and automatically blocks rendering until the font is ready.
00013| 
00014| ### Prerequisites
00015| 
00016| First, the @remotion/google-fonts package needs to be installed.
00017| If it is not installed, use the following command:
00018| 
00019| ```bash
00020| npx remotion add @remotion/google-fonts # If project uses npm
00021| bunx remotion add @remotion/google-fonts # If project uses bun
00022| yarn remotion add @remotion/google-fonts # If project uses yarn
00023| pnpm exec remotion add @remotion/google-fonts # If project uses pnpm
00024| ```
00025| 
00026| ```tsx
00027| import { loadFont } from "@remotion/google-fonts/Lobster";
00028| 
00029| const { fontFamily } = loadFont();
00030| 
00031| export const MyComposition = () => {
00032|   return <div style={{ fontFamily }}>Hello World</div>;
00033| };
00034| ```
00035| 
00036| Preferrably, specify only needed weights and subsets to reduce file size:
00037| 
00038| ```tsx
00039| import { loadFont } from "@remotion/google-fonts/Roboto";
00040| 
00041| const { fontFamily } = loadFont("normal", {
00042|   weights: ["400", "700"],
00043|   subsets: ["latin"],
00044| });
00045| ```
00046| 
00047| ### Waiting for font to load
00048| 
00049| Use `waitUntilDone()` if you need to know when the font is ready:
00050| 
00051| ```tsx
00052| import { loadFont } from "@remotion/google-fonts/Lobster";
00053| 
00054| const { fontFamily, waitUntilDone } = loadFont();
00055| 
00056| await waitUntilDone();
00057| ```
00058| 
00059| ## Local fonts with @remotion/fonts
00060| 
00061| For local font files, use the `@remotion/fonts` package.
00062| 
00063| ### Prerequisites
00064| 
00065| First, install @remotion/fonts:
00066| 
00067| ```bash
00068| npx remotion add @remotion/fonts # If project uses npm
00069| bunx remotion add @remotion/fonts # If project uses bun
00070| yarn remotion add @remotion/fonts # If project uses yarn
00071| pnpm exec remotion add @remotion/fonts # If project uses pnpm
00072| ```
00073| 
00074| ### Loading a local font
00075| 
00076| Place your font file in the `public/` folder and use `loadFont()`:
00077| 
00078| ```tsx
00079| import { loadFont } from "@remotion/fonts";
00080| import { staticFile } from "remotion";
00081| 
00082| await loadFont({
00083|   family: "MyFont",
00084|   url: staticFile("MyFont-Regular.woff2"),
00085| });
00086| 
00087| export const MyComposition = () => {
00088|   return <div style={{ fontFamily: "MyFont" }}>Hello World</div>;
00089| };
00090| ```
00091| 
00092| ### Loading multiple weights
00093| 
00094| Load each weight separately with the same family name:
00095| 
00096| ```tsx
00097| import { loadFont } from "@remotion/fonts";
00098| import { staticFile } from "remotion";
00099| 
00100| await Promise.all([
00101|   loadFont({
00102|     family: "Inter",
00103|     url: staticFile("Inter-Regular.woff2"),
00104|     weight: "400",
00105|   }),
00106|   loadFont({
00107|     family: "Inter",
00108|     url: staticFile("Inter-Bold.woff2"),
00109|     weight: "700",
00110|   }),
00111| ]);
00112| ```
00113| 
00114| ### Available options
00115| 
00116| ```tsx
00117| loadFont({
00118|   family: "MyFont", // Required: name to use in CSS
00119|   url: staticFile("font.woff2"), // Required: font file URL
00120|   format: "woff2", // Optional: auto-detected from extension
00121|   weight: "400", // Optional: font weight
00122|   style: "normal", // Optional: normal or italic
00123|   display: "block", // Optional: font-display behavior
00124| });
00125| ```
00126| 
00127| ## Using in components
00128| 
00129| Call `loadFont()` at the top level of your component or in a separate file that's imported early:
00130| 
00131| ```tsx
00132| import { loadFont } from "@remotion/google-fonts/Montserrat";
00133| 
00134| const { fontFamily } = loadFont("normal", {
00135|   weights: ["400", "700"],
00136|   subsets: ["latin"],
00137| });
00138| 
00139| export const Title: React.FC<{ text: string }> = ({ text }) => {
00140|   return (
00141|     <h1
00142|       style={{
00143|         fontFamily,
00144|         fontSize: 80,
00145|         fontWeight: "bold",
00146|       }}
00147|     >
00148|       {text}
00149|     </h1>
00150|   );
00151| };
00152| ```

00001| ---
00002| name: compositions
00003| description: Defining compositions, stills, folders, default props and dynamic metadata
00004| metadata:
00005|   tags: composition, still, folder, props, metadata
00006| ---
00007| 
00008| A `<Composition>` defines the component, width, height, fps and duration of a renderable video.
00009| 
00010| It normally is placed in the `src/Root.tsx` file.
00011| 
00012| ```tsx
00013| import { Composition } from "remotion";
00014| import { MyComposition } from "./MyComposition";
00015| 
00016| export const RemotionRoot = () => {
00017|   return (
00018|     <Composition
00019|       id="MyComposition"
00020|       component={MyComposition}
00021|       durationInFrames={100}
00022|       fps={30}
00023|       width={1080}
00024|       height={1080}
00025|     />
00026|   );
00027| };
00028| ```
00029| 
00030| ## Default Props
00031| 
00032| Pass `defaultProps` to provide initial values for your component.  
00033| Values must be JSON-serializable (`Date`, `Map`, `Set`, and `staticFile()` are supported).
00034| 
00035| ```tsx
00036| import { Composition } from "remotion";
00037| import { MyComposition, MyCompositionProps } from "./MyComposition";
00038| 
00039| export const RemotionRoot = () => {
00040|   return (
00041|     <Composition
00042|       id="MyComposition"
00043|       component={MyComposition}
00044|       durationInFrames={100}
00045|       fps={30}
00046|       width={1080}
00047|       height={1080}
00048|       defaultProps={{
00049|         title: "Hello World",
00050|         color: "#ff0000",
00051|       } satisfies MyCompositionProps}
00052|     />
00053|   );
00054| };
00055| ```
00056| 
00057| Use `type` declarations for props rather than `interface` to ensure `defaultProps` type safety.
00058| 
00059| ## Folders
00060| 
00061| Use `<Folder>` to organize compositions in the sidebar.  
00062| Folder names can only contain letters, numbers, and hyphens.
00063| 
00064| ```tsx
00065| import { Composition, Folder } from "remotion";
00066| 
00067| export const RemotionRoot = () => {
00068|   return (
00069|     <>
00070|       <Folder name="Marketing">
00071|         <Composition id="Promo" /* ... */ />
00072|         <Composition id="Ad" /* ... */ />
00073|       </Folder>
00074|       <Folder name="Social">
00075|         <Folder name="Instagram">
00076|           <Composition id="Story" /* ... */ />
00077|           <Composition id="Reel" /* ... */ />
00078|         </Folder>
00079|       </Folder>
00080|     </>
00081|   );
00082| };
00083| ```
00084| 
00085| ## Stills
00086| 
00087| Use `<Still>` for single-frame images. It does not require `durationInFrames` or `fps`.
00088| 
00089| ```tsx
00090| import { Still } from "remotion";
00091| import { Thumbnail } from "./Thumbnail";
00092| 
00093| export const RemotionRoot = () => {
00094|   return (
00095|     <Still
00096|       id="Thumbnail"
00097|       component={Thumbnail}
00098|       width={1280}
00099|       height={720}
00100|     />
00101|   );
00102| };
00103| ```
00104| 
00105| ## Calculate Metadata
00106| 
00107| Use `calculateMetadata` to make dimensions, duration, or props dynamic based on data.
00108| 
00109| ```tsx
00110| import { Composition, CalculateMetadataFunction } from "remotion";
00111| import { MyComposition, MyCompositionProps } from "./MyComposition";
00112| 
00113| const calculateMetadata: CalculateMetadataFunction<MyCompositionProps> = async ({
00114|   props,
00115|   abortSignal,
00116| }) => {
00117|   const data = await fetch(`https://api.example.com/video/${props.videoId}`, {
00118|     signal: abortSignal,
00119|   }).then((res) => res.json());
00120| 
00121|   return {
00122|     durationInFrames: Math.ceil(data.duration * 30),
00123|     props: {
00124|       ...props,
00125|       videoUrl: data.url,
00126|     },
00127|   };
00128| };
00129| 
00130| export const RemotionRoot = () => {
00131|   return (
00132|     <Composition
00133|       id="MyComposition"
00134|       component={MyComposition}
00135|       durationInFrames={100} // Placeholder, will be overridden
00136|       fps={30}
00137|       width={1080}
00138|       height={1080}
00139|       defaultProps={{ videoId: "abc123" }}
00140|       calculateMetadata={calculateMetadata}
00141|     />
00142|   );
00143| };
00144| ```
00145| 
00146| The function can return `props`, `durationInFrames`, `width`, `height`, `fps`, and codec-related defaults. It runs once before rendering begins.

00020| const getTypedText = ({
00021| 	frame,
00022| 	fullText,
00023| 	pauseAfter,
00024| 	charFrames,
00025| 	pauseFrames,
00026| }: {
00027| 	frame: number;
00028| 	fullText: string;
00029| 	pauseAfter: string;
00030| 	charFrames: number;
00031| 	pauseFrames: number;
00032| }): string => {
00033| 	const pauseIndex = fullText.indexOf(pauseAfter);
00034| 	const preLen =

00059| 		[0, blinkFrames / 2, blinkFrames],

  "content": "import {\n  AbsoluteFill,\n  interpolate,\n  spring,\n  useCurrentFrame,\n  useVideoConfig,\n} from \"remotion\";\n\nconst ASCII_LOGO = `███████╗██╗  ██╗██╗██╗     ██╗     ███████╗\n██╔════╝██║ ██╔╝██║██║     ██║     ██╔════╝\n███████╗█████╔╝ ██║██║     ██║     ███████╗\n╚════██║██╔═██╗ ██║██║     ██║     ╚════██║\n███████║██║  ██╗██║███████╗███████╗███████║\n╚══════╝╚═╝  ╚═╝╚═╝╚══════╝╚══════╝╚══════╝`;\n\nexport const AsciiLogoScene = () => {\n  const frame = useCurrentFrame();\n  const { fps } = useVideoConfig();\n\n  // Reveal animation - characters appear one by one\n  const lines = ASCII_LOGO.split(\"\\n\");\n  const totalChars = ASCII_LOGO.length;\n  const revealProgress = interpolate(frame, [0, 1.5 * fps], [0, 1], {\n    extrapolateRight: \"clamp\",\n  });\n  const charsToShow = Math.floor(revealProgress * totalChars);\n\n  // After reveal, pulse glow effect\n  const glowIntensity = spring({\n    frame: frame - 2 * fps,\n    fps,\n    config: { damping: 10, stiffness: 80 },\n  });\n\n  // Scale entrance\n  const scale = spring({\n    frame,\n    fps,\n    config: { damping: 200 },\n  });\n\n  // Build revealed text\n  let charCount = 0;\n  const revealedLines = lines.map((line) => {\n    let revealedLine = \"\";\n    for (const char of line) {\n      if (charCount < charsToShow) {\n        revealedLine += char;\n      } else {\n        revealedLine += \" \";\n      }\n      charCount++;\n    }\n    charCount++; // for newline\n    return revealedLine;\n  });\n\n  return (\n    <AbsoluteFill\n      style={{\n        backgroundColor: \"#fafafa\",\n        justifyContent: \"center\",\n        alignItems: \"center\",\n      }}\n    >\n      {/* Subtle gradient background */}\n      <div\n        style={{\n          position: \"absolute\",\n          inset: 0,\n          background:\n            \"radial-gradient(ellipse at center, rgba(0,0,0,0.02) 0%, transparent 70%)\",\n        }}\n      />\n\n      <div\n        style={{\n          transform: `scale(${scale})`,\n          display: \"flex\",\n          flexDirection: \"column\",\n          alignItems: \"center\",\n        }}\n      >\n        <pre\n          style={{\n            fontFamily: \"monospace\",\n            fontSize: 32,\n            fontWeight: 700,\n            lineHeight: 1.1,\n            color: \"#111\",\n            textShadow:\n              glowIntensity > 0\n                ? `0 0 ${20 * glowIntensity}px rgba(0,0,0,0.15)`\n                : \"none\",\n            letterSpacing: -1,\n          }}\n        >\n          {revealedLines.join(\"\\n\")}\n        </pre>\n\n        {/* Tagline */}\n        <div\n          style={{\n            marginTop: 60,\n            opacity: interpolate(frame, [2 * fps, 2.5 * fps], [0, 1], {\n              extrapolateLeft: \"clamp\",\n              extrapolateRight: \"clamp\",\n            }),\n            transform: `translateY(${interpolate(\n              frame,\n              [2 * fps, 2.5 * fps],\n              [20, 0],\n              {\n                extrapolateLeft: \"clamp\",\n                extrapolateRight: \"clamp\",\n              }\n            )}px)`,\n          }}\n        >\n          <p\n            style={{\n              fontSize: 48,\n              fontWeight: 500,\n     </p>\n        </div>\n      </div>\n    </AbsoluteFill>\n  );\n};\n"

## Video Structure (25 seconds, 9:16 vertical)

**Scene 1 - ASCII Logo (4s)**
- Character-by-character reveal of the SKILLS ASCII art
- Spring scale entrance with subtle glow pulse
- Tagline fades in: "The Open Agent Skills Ecosystem"

**Scene 2 - Terminal Install (5s)**  
- macOS-style terminal window animates in
- Typewriter effect: `npx skills add <owner/repo>`
- Success message appears after typing completes

**Scene 3 - Agent Carousel (4s)**
- Header: "Works with all your favorite agents"
- 12 agent pills bounce in with staggered delays
- Subtle floating animation on each pill
- Counter: "16+ AI agents supported"

**Scene 4 - Leaderboard (8s)**
- Shows top 7 skills from skills.sh
- Each row slides in with animated install counts
- Top 3 get prominent styling

**Scene 5 - CTA (4s)**
- "Visit" springs in
- "skills.sh" with highlight wipe animation
- "today" fades up
- Subtle pulse effect on the URL

## How to use

```bash
cd skills-video

# Preview in browser
npm run dev          # Opens at http://localhost:3004

# Render final video
npm run build        # Outputs to out/video.mp4
